PREFACE 
This thesis is neither my best nor worst work, IвҖҷve ever done in my professional life; 
however, most probably the last one, related with my profession. As jobless and hopeless, 
I wish, this work would be beneficial someone, somehow, somewhere, sometimeвҖҰ 
==PAGE:8==
ABSTRACT 
This Report concerns to develop a generic VSC HVDC Controller Model with different 
active and reactive control modes, which defined in ENTSO-EвҖҷs HVDC Grid Code, in 
the light of guidance of Cigre 604.2014, for using in RMS simulation of DigSilent 
PowerFactory to analyze frequency and voltage support of VSC HVDC. Since in future 
these supports will be crucial for survivals of grids, where biggest share of electric power 
may be supplied by static sources, which connected to grid via DC/AC converters, under 
even smaller disturbances. 
Therefore, the report begins with definitions, how a grid should be called strong or weak, 
and conventional source of the defined strength; and continues with pointing out issues 
between weak grid and older LCC HVDC technology and near future requirements of 
grid regulators to emphasize of the need of such a report. 
Before analyzing supports of developed active & reactive power control modes to a weak 
grid, some steps should be achieved. First, generic model must be developed, whose total 
model is explained in detail with a brief introduction of VSC Controller technology and 
system components, second the generic model has to be tested with issued cases to prove 
its convenience.  
Afterwards, synchronous generators are implemented instead of using ideal voltage 
sources; for enabling this implementation and making relevant definition of weak gridвҖҷs 
threat, which caused by static & dynamic source-mix, an alternative grid is introduced; 
and previous, same cases are re-investigated with the alternative grid. 
Last a new simple weak grid is represented, to analyze effectiveness of new active and 
reactive power control modes, such as Frequency Sensitivity Mode (FSM), Synthetic 
Inertia and AC Voltage Droop, under disturbances, e.g. sudden active power increase and 
load rejection in the system. With different level fault events, categorized via caused 
voltage drop, Fault-Ride-Through (FRT) capability and Short-Circuit Contribution of 
converter is examined, too. 
The report is concluded with some highlighted results, discussions about transformation 
of power system and future work requirement.

INTRODUCTION 
1 
1 
INTRODUCTION 
In this chapter a brief introduction to the background and purpose for performing this 
master thesis is described. 
1.1 Background of the problem 
The share of renewable and distributed energy resources (DERs) used for electric power 
generation will further increase in the future, to reach the renewable energy goals, set by 
several countries around the world. The power generation of those energy sources is 
depending on the weather conditions, e.g. solar radiation and wind. Moreover, the 
majority is connected to the network through power electronics. This has an impact on 
the inertia and the short-circuit power of a power system. When DERs are dominantly 
used and replace conventional power generation, system inertia and short-circuit power 
is low. While during times with low penetration from DERs and power production 
dominated by conventional generators, the inertia and short-circuit power is higher. Such 
a variation in the system greatly impacts the dynamic response of a power system, e.g. in 
case of a contingency, and is challenging the existing control and protection schemes. An 
example is that Frequency Containment Reserves may be triggered late or may become 
insufficient in size or that, due to current limitations in power electronics, protection relay 
settings may be no longer capable of identifying short circuits. 
The current solution to ensure secure and stable operation of the system is to require a 
certain number of conventional generators to be connected and additional installation of 
synchronous condensers providing voltage support and short-circuit power. 
1.2 Thesis Objectives & Scope 
1) Investigate the function of inertia and short-circuit power in electric power systems  
2) Identify characteristics of rotating machines (incl. synchronous generators and large 
machine loads), which impact system behavior. 
3) Assess which components in the system are dependent on short-circuit power and 
inertia. Describe what are the problems and limits.  
4) Review the regulatorsвҖҷ perspective  
a) Current regulations about synthetic inertia & short-circuit current supports  
b) Assessments & reports for future needs  
==PAGE:22==
5) Reviewing LCC & VSC technologies and their abilities to support the grid with 
synthetic inertia & short-circuit current.  
6) Implement a generic VSC model for dynamic simulations in Powerfactory  
7) Evaluation of the impact of VSC HVDC operated in different control modes on the 
stability of a power system, where inertia and short-circuit power is varying 
a) Contribution to short-circuit currents in different operational conditions  
b) Inertia and fast-frequency response to an active power disturbance  
1.3 Learning Objectives 
1) Discuss the impact of distributed energy resources on the inertia and short-circuit 
power in a power system  
2) Describe the dynamic behavior of rotating machines in power systems and their 
contribution to system inertia and short-circuit power  
3) Identify and list components in a power system impacted by variation of system 
inertia and short-circuit power  
4) Explain and compare the capabilities of LCC and VSC HVDC technology to support 
a system with synthetic inertia & short-circuit current  
5) Implement a generic VSC HVDC model in the power system simulation software 
Powerfactory  
6) Create a controller for VSC HVDC to support a system, where inertia and short-circuit 
power are low  
7) Assess the impact of the VSC HVDC and the controller on the stability of the power 
system 
1.4 Readability 
ThesisвҖҷ chapter organization and brief description about chaptersвҖҷ content are given 
below: 
Chapter 1 is an introduction to Thesis, background and objectives are given here. 
Chapter 2 is presenting some definitions about strength of grid, as well as is identifying 
dynamic characteristic of synchronous generator and static sources under a disturbance. 
Chapter 3 is focusing both issues between weak grid and classical LCC HVDC systems 
and traditional solutions to them. 
Chapter 4 is based on requirements of ENTSO-E about both HVDC implementation and 
future grid operation. 
Chapter 5 is covering VSC technologies and VSC model description of Cigre 604. 
Chapter 6 is about detailed and complete description of VSC HVDC controller modelled 
in DigSilent. 
==PAGE:23==
 
INTRODUCTION 
3 
Chapter 7 is testing the created VSC controller model with result of an issued article. 
Chapter 8 is recommending an alternative grid to the grid used in Chapter 7, where 
implementation of synchronous generator is possible. 
Chapter 9 is containing simulations and analysis focusing frequency response and short-
circuit contribution of VSC HVDC unit. 
Chapter 10 is conclusion of Thesis, which contains some highlights and remarks to results 
and future grid. 
==PAGE:24==
==PAGE:25==
 
STRONG GRID vs. WEAK GRID 
5 
2 
STRONG GRID vs. WEAK GRID 
Contrary conventional power plants, in the future there will be more wind, solar and 
small-scale hydropower connected to the power grid. The consumption characteristics 
will also change, for example more induction motor will be connected via frequency 
converters to the grid and the connection power-capacity between synchronous areas will 
increase with new HVDC links, especially in the Nordic Region of ENTSO-E. All those 
changes will affect the strength of the power system. [1]  
2.1 Definitions of the Strength of Grid 
From the perspective of early application of HVDC, planners or designers have been 
defining the grid as вҖҳweakвҖҷ, if the equivalent impedance of the grid at the point of HVDC 
connection (PCC вҖ“ point of common coupling) relative to the DC power is high or the 
inertia of the AC-Grid is low. [2] 
An AC-Grid can be defined as вҖҳweakвҖҷ from two aspects: [2] 
a) AC grid impedance may be high relative to DC power at the PCC. 
b) AC grid mechanical inertia may be inadequate relative to the DC power infeed. 
2.1.1 The Grid Impedance 
First, it is needed to give some definition of Short Circuit Ratios: 
Short Circuit Ratio (SCR): [2] 
ЬөЬҘЬҙ= Ьө
ЬІаҜ—а¬ө
 
(2-1) 
 
ЬөаҜҰаҜҰаҜ–: the AC system 3Я¶ symmetrical short-circuit level in MVA at the convertor 
terminal AC bus with 1.0 pu AC terminal voltage. 
ЬІаҜ—а¬ө: the rated DC terminal power in MW 
Effective Short Circuit Ratio (ESCR): [2] 
Shunt capacitors including AC filters connected at the AC terminal of a DC link can 
significantly increase the effective AC system impedance. 
==PAGE:26==
Ь§ЬөЬҘЬҙ= ЬөаҜҰаҜҰаҜ–вҲ’ЬіаҜ–
ЬІаҜ—а¬ө
 
(2-2) 
 
ЬіаҜ–: the value of 3Я¶ fundamental MVAr in per unit of ЬІаҜ—а¬ө at per unit AC voltage of shunt 
capacitors connected to the convertor AC bars (AC filters and plain shunt banks) 
Following Short Circuit Ratio (SCR) values can be used to classify the strength of AC/DC 
system. SCR is the ratio of AC-GridвҖҷs short-circuit capacity to the connected HVDC 
power вҖ“ if itвҖҷs lower, so the interaction between AC/DC will be greater. [2] 
пӮ· 
A high SCR AC/DC System is categorized by an SCR value greater than 3. 
пӮ· 
A low SCR AC/DC System is categorized by an SCR value between 2 and 3. 
пӮ· 
A very low SCR AC/DC System is categorized by an SCR value lower than 2. 
2.1.2 The Grid Inertia 
Traditionally, power system operation is based on electricity generation, in the form of 
thermal power or hydro plants, is fully controllable, and involves rotating synchronous 
generators. Via their stored kinetic energy, they add rotational inertia, an important 
property of frequency dynamics and stability. The contribution of inertia is an inherent 
and crucial feature of rotating synchronous generators. [3] 
For satisfactory performance, the AC system should have a minimum inertia relative to 
the size of the DC connection. [4] 
ЬӘаҜ—аҜ–= ЭҗЭӢЭҗЬҪЭҲЭҺЭӢЭҗЬҪЭҗЭ…ЭӢЭҠЬҪЭҲЭ…ЭҠЭҒЭҺЭҗЭ…ЬҪЭӢЭӮЬЈЬҘЭҸЭ•ЭҸЭҗЭҒЭүЬҜЬ№ЭҸ
ЬҜЬ№ЭҺЬҪЭҗЭ…ЭҠЭғЭӢЭӮЬҰЬҘЭҲЭ…ЭҠЭҮ
 
(2-3) 
 
An effective inertia constant, ЬӘаҜ—аҜ–, of at least 2.0 to 3.0ЭҸ is required for satisfactory 
operation. [4] 
2.2 Conventional Source of Inertia and Short-Circuit Power (by 
Rotating Machines) 
The main components of a synchronous generator, which is source of strength of 
conventional grids, are: [5] 
пӮ· The stator is the stationary part, made up in cylindrical form, provided on the 
inner surface with equidistant slots recessed by the windings. 
пӮ· 
The rotor is the mobile part, which contains a field (excitation) winding, 
supplied with a direct current to produce a magnetic field stationary to the rotor 
and damper windings. 
==PAGE:27==
 
STRONG GRID vs. WEAK GRID 
7 
 
Figure 2-1: Schematic diagram of a three-phase synchronous machine [5] 
2.2.1 Electromagnetic Model 
Stator Circuits: The voltages at the stator winding terminals are Э’аҜ”, Э’аҜ• and Э’аҜ–, and the 
currents are Э…аҜ”, Э…аҜ• and Э…аҜ–. [5] 
Rotor Circuits: The field (excitation) winding ЭӮвҖ“ ЭӮбҮұis taken as the direct axis, d-axis, and 
the quadrature axis, q-axis. The damper windings are disposed on the two rotor axes, the 
damper winding in the d-axis, D, and one in the q-axis, Q. These windings are 
permanently short-circuited. [5] 
 
Figure 2-2: The circuits of the synchronous generator: rotor circuit and stator circuit [5] 
The Park transformation is implemented to replace the three stator windings a, b and c by 
three fictitious rotor windings called d, q, 0 (rotor coordinates system) [5] 
пӮ· The windings disposed in the d-axis and q-axis are rotating together with the 
rotor, and there are no mutual couplings between them. 
пӮ· The 0-axis is independent of the d-axis and q-axis since zero-sequence currents 
flow through it only in unbalanced conditions.

2.2.1.2 Transient Processes or States in Synchronous Generator 
The rotating machines are the main sources of short-circuit currents. The flux linking each 
armature winding is trapped at the instant of short-circuit occurrence. [5] 
i. 
Stator transient states are associated with the transformer voltages, which 
generate DC components of the stator phase currents during a short circuit. 
ii. 
Rotor transient states are associated with the terms 
аӯўа®Ёаұң
аӯўаӯІ, 
аӯўа®ЁаұҖ
аӯўаӯІ, and so on, of the 
rotor windings equations. Two dynamic behaviors are identified: 
a. subtransient dynamic response, associated with the damper windings and 
eddy currents; 
b. transient dynamic response, associated with the field winding; 
iii. 
Mechanical states associated with the shaft motion. (Electromechanical Model) 
2.2.2 Electromechanical Model of Synchronous Generator: Swing 
Equation 
The inertia of a power system was defined as the ability of a system to oppose changes in 
frequency due to resistance provided by kinetic energy of rotating masses. If a power 
system is subjected to an imbalance between power production and consumption, the 
system frequency changes. This frequency change is a result of the synchronously 
connected generators accelerating or decelerating. The kinetic energy stored in rotating 
==PAGE:30==
masses in the system is dependent on their rotational speed, which begins to change. The 
change in frequency results in a change of electrical power generated by the generators. 
This change in electrical power is often referred to as inertial response as the change in 
electrical power comes from the change in kinetic energy stored in rotating masses. [1] 
The swing equation describes the acceleration (deceleration) of the synchronous 
generator and turbine (prime mover) due to any imbalance between mechanical torque 
and electromagnetic torque: [5]

STRONG GRID vs. WEAK GRID

2.3 Situation of Static Sources 
2.3.1 Short-Circuit Contribution 
IEC 60909 is introducing two short-circuit currents. The maximum short-circuit current 
is responsible for the rating of equipment regarding the mechanical and thermal stresses, 
while the minimum short-circuit current is for the protection settings. [6] 
The method used for calculation is based on the introduction of an equivalent voltage 
source at the short-circuit location. The equivalent voltage source is the only active 
voltage of the system. All network feeders, synchronous and asynchronous machines are 
replaced by their internal impedances. [6] 
Power stations units with full size converter, e.g. wind power station unit and photovoltaic 
station units are modelled in the positive-sequence system by a current source. The 
positive-sequence shunt impedance ЬјаҜүа®ҝ is assumed to be infinite. [6] 
The contribution of power station units with full size converter to the maximum initial 
short-circuit current shall be calculated as follows: [6]

аҜЎ
аҜқаӯҖа¬ө
 
(2-26)

ЬјаҜңаҜқ: the absolute value of the elements of the nodal impedance matrix of the positive-
sequence system. Э… is the short-circuit node and ЭҶ are the nodes where power station 
units with full size converters are connected 
Ь«аҜҰаҜһаҜүа®ҝаҜқ: the RMS value of the maximum source current (positive-sequence system) 
When calculating minimum short-circuit currents, contributions wind and photovoltaic 
power stations shall be neglected. [6] 
2.3.2 Inertial Response 
Due to non-synchronously connected production units, like modern wind turbine 
generators, their rotational speed is isolated from the system frequency. They therefore 
do not deliver a natural inertial response and do not contribute to the system inertia [1]. 
Or there isnвҖҷt any rotational speed, e.g. PV units, so they cannot deliver a natural inertial 
response. 
Inertial response produced by a controller is often called to as a synthetic inertial response. 
[1] 
==PAGE:32==
==PAGE:33==
 
ISSUES with WEAK GRID 
13 
3 
ISSUES with WEAK GRID 
3.1 Issue about Grid Protection 
Grids are going to be weaker, if less conventional synchronous generator is going to be 
directly connected to the grid. It is, what renewable energy transformation is causing. [7] 
Although it is expected an increase in short-circuit capacity due to gridвҖҷs assets 
improvement, there is also consideration about a decrease in short-circuit level due to 
replacement of conventional synchronous generation by inverter coupled generating units 
[7], which are supplying short-circuit current as a current source, rather than a voltage 
source, if they have such a capability [6]. 
3.2 Issues about LCC-HVDC 
3.2.1 Affecting to LCC-HVDC  
The following are the problems associated with operation of LCC HVDC system when 
connected to a weak AC grid: [4] 
a. High dynamic overvoltage вҖ“ temporary overvoltage (TOV) [2] 
When there is an interruption to the DC power transfer, the reactive power absorption of 
the HVDC converters drop to zero. With a low ESCR system, the resulting increase in 
alternating voltage due to shunt capacitors and harmonic filters could be excessive. This 
will require a high insulation level of terminal equipment or affects surge arrester ratings. 
[2] [4] 
b. Voltage instability 
The LCC-HVDC station always consumes reactive power in the range of 0.5 to 0.6 p.u. 
of transmitted power (very sensitive to changes in loading [4]). The amount consumed 
depends on the commutation reactance and operating Яҷ and Яӣ but is influenced only 
marginally by the power flow direction (rectifier or inverter), particularly on the inverter 
side [4]. [2] 
cos Я¶вүҲcos ЯҷвҲ’Ь«аҜ—
ЬёаҜ—а¬ҙ
3
ЯЁЬәаҜ– 
(3-1) 
 
==PAGE:34==
An increase in direct current is accompanied by a fall of alternating voltage. 
Consequently, the actual increase in power may be small or negligible, so control of 
voltage and recovery from disturbances become difficult. The sensitivity increases with 
large amounts of shunt capacitors. [4] 
c. Harmonic resonance 
Shunt capacitors are used for AC filters and for reactive power supply. The larger the 
ratio of shunt capacitor MVAr to AC system short circuit MVA, the lower will be the 
resonant frequency for parallel resonance. [2] [4] 
d.  Objectionable voltage flicker 
The transient voltage flicker due to frequently switched reactive devices increase with 
higher levels of DC power transfer. [4] 
3.2.2 Affected by LCC-HVDC  
If AC system receives all or most of its power from a DC connection, the inertia of the 
receiving AC system may be inadequate, so that upon the interruption of the DC infeed, 
due to any cause, the system voltage and frequency may decrease to unacceptably low 
values. [2] 
3.3 Conventional Coping Mechanisms 
a. Short-Circuit Protection: 
In case a fault occurs in the grid, nearby a reduced short-circuit power capacity because 
of transformation of generation, there will be a lack of necessary voltage support, which 
cause flattening of the voltage cone, so farther generators can contribute with higher 
short-circuit currents due to lower voltages at their grid connection points. [7] 
Grid enforcement is reducing the Thevenin equivalent impedance [6] in some degree; as 
well as, it enhances the effect of contribution of more generation units to the fault, because 
they will lead to a tighter coupling between the remaining generators and will decrease 
the electrical distance between generators and fault locations. [7] 
In addition, the effects of changing short-circuit power as well as changing voltage 
profiles during failures should be carefully analyzed to readjust protection settings of used 
protection equipment. [7] 
b. Reactive Power Compensation:  
The least expensive way to provide the required reactive power is to use shunt capacitor 
banks. The stronger the AC grid, the larger the switchable bank size can be for an 
acceptable voltage change. [4] 
==PAGE:35==
 
ISSUES with WEAK GRID 
15 
For weak AC systems, it may be necessary to provide reactive compensation in the form 
of static VAr compensators (SVCs) or synchronous condensers. [4] 
c. Temporary Overvoltage (TOV): 
In early schemes, the problem of too high TOV was solved by the addition of synchronous 
compensators in the inverter stations, i.e. by the reduction of the AC system impedance 
as seen by the LCC-HVDC convertor. The application of metal-oxide arrestors has been 
made to control TOV without the need for synchronous compensators. [2] 
d. Voltage Stability: 
The traditional approach to the solution of weak system AC/DC interaction problems is 
to use synchronous condensers or static VAr compensators SVCs. In addition, LCC-
HVDC controls which switch to current control from power control and reduce direct 
current for low alternating voltage will help the situation. [4] 
e. Low Kinetic Energy: 
In addition to voltage stability, if an LCC-HVDC inverter is supplying an вҖҳisland systemвҖҷ, 
synchronous condensers, having adequate inertia, have to be used to strengthen the AC 
system to maintain the frequency and voltage to an acceptable level during system faults. 
The system inertia constant referred to DC power, ЬӘаҜ—аҜ–, should for example, be greater 
than 2ЭҸ to maintain frequency deviation under fault conditions within 5%. [2]  
==PAGE:36==
4 
FUTURE GRID REQUIREMENT вҖ“ 
REGULATORSвҖҷ PERSPECTIVE  
4.1 General Requirements for HVDC by ENTSO-E 
In this chapter, issued requirements by ENTSO-E for grid connection of HVDC system, 
which are important for generic modeling and simulations, are summarized. 
4.1.1 Requirements for active power control and frequency support 
4.1.1.1 Rate-of-change-of-frequency withstand capability 
HVDC system shall stay connected to the network and operable if the network frequency 
changes at a rate between вҖ“ 2,5 and + 2,5 Hz/s [8] 
4.1.1.2 Active power controllability, control range and ramping rate 
HVDC system shall be controllable to take automatic remedial actions, e.g. stopping the 
ramping and blocking FSM, LFSM-O, LFSM-U and frequency control. [8] 
4.1.1.3 Synthetic inertia 
An HVDC system shall be capable of providing synthetic inertia in response to frequency 
changes, activated in low and/or high frequency regimes by rapidly adjusting the active 
power injected to or withdrawn from the AC network in order to limit the rate of change 
of frequency. [8] 
4.1.1.4 Frequency control 
An HVDC system shall be equipped with an independent control mode to modulate the 
active power output of the HVDC converter station depending on the frequencies at all 
connection points of the HVDC system in order to maintain stable system frequencies. 
[8]

4.1.2 Requirements for reactive power control and voltage support 
4.1.2.1 Short circuit contribution during faults 
An HVDC system shall have the capability to provide fast fault current at a connection 
point in case of symmetrical (3-phase) faults. [8] 
4.1.2.2 Reactive power capability 
An HVDC converter station shall be capable of operating in one or more of the three 
following control modes; (a) voltage control mode, (b) reactive power control mode, (c) 
power factor control mode. [8]

4.1.4 Power oscillation damping capability 
The HVDC system shall be capable of contributing to the damping of power oscillations 
in connected AC networks. The control system of the HVDC system shall not reduce the 
damping of power oscillations. [8] 
4.2 Nordic Requirements for Frequency Response 
There are Nordic-Grid specific requirements for frequency control, too. 
The start of the frequency disturbance is defined as the time when absolute value of the 
ЭҖЭӮ/ЭҖЭҗ or RoCoF (Rate of Change of Frequency), exceeds 0.035 ЬӘЭ–/ЭҸ, which was chosen 
for the threshold after performing an empirical analysis. [1] 
 
Figure 4-6: Graphical Representation of Frequency Response Indicators 
About the contribution of generators to the kinetic energy of the system, it is assumed that 
they are contributing if their circuit breakers are closed. The kinetic energy capacity of 
the Nordic power system is calculated with previous assumption and the equation below, 
which is 390 GWs. [1]

VSC TECHNOLOGY & GENERIC VSC MODEL 
23 
5 
VSC TECHNOLOGY & GENERIC VSC MODEL 
5.1 VSC Technology 
The VSC-HVDC system is a relatively mature technology that comprises the high-power, 
high-frequency semiconductor switches (i.e., IGBTs and GTOs). These devices 
incorporated with antiparallel diodes make one complete unit. Several units are connected 
in series to build a valve to get the required voltage level and to increase the redundancy 
in the converter. The control of these switches is done by using pulse-width modulation 
(PWM) techniques by which it is possible to control the magnitude and phase angle of 
the generated fundamental voltage component. [10] 
 
Figure 5-1: Single-line diagram of VSC-HVDC system 
Components of VSC-HVDC System, seen in the Figure 5-1, are briefly described 
following parts. 
5.1.1 AC Shunt RLC-Filters 
Switching of high-power, high-frequency switches generates harmonics in the converter 
output voltages and currents. The order of harmonics generated is directly related to the 
PWM switching frequency of the semiconductor switches. Single- or double-tuned low-
pass and high-pass damped RLC filters are connected to suppress these harmonics. [10] 
5.1.2 Converter Transformer 
It provides electric isolation and operates as a filter between converter and AC networks 
and provides the appropriate AC voltage level to optimize the available converter valve 
voltage rating. [10] 
==PAGE:44==
5.1.3 Voltage Source Converter 
The number of switches employed depends on the operating characteristic and voltage 
level required. The series-connected IGBT switches, connected with antiparallel diodes, 
make up a valve. Two valves are connected in series to make up the converter leg for one 
phase. [10] 
5.1.3.1 IGBT 
IGBT is a device having features of BJT with high voltage withstanding capability and 
of MOSFET with high speed switching capability and of GTO with self-commutation 
characteristics. 
The IGBT has high impedance gate, which requires a small amount of energy to switch 
the device. The IGBT has a small ON state voltage (Э’аҜўаҜЎ= 2 вҲ’3Ьё), which creates the 
ON state losses, even in devices with large blocking voltage ratings of 1,000 V. IGBT 
turn-on and turn-off times is in the order of 1 ЭүЭҸ and typically, available large module 
rating is 4.5ЭҮЬё, 1,500ЬЈ with a switching frequency of 20 ЭҮЬӘЭ–. [11] 
 
Figure 5-2: IGBT the Symbol and v - i characteristics 
5.1.3.2 Snubber Circuits 
The switching losses are the second major loss mechanism during the turn-on and turn-
off transition. In the case of a device switch, very small leakage current Э…аҜҹаҜҳаҜ”аҜһ would 
continue to flow at turn-on state, as well as, very small leakage voltage Э’аҜ”аҜ•вү 0 exists at 
turn-off state. [11] 
==PAGE:45==
 
VSC TECHNOLOGY & GENERIC VSC MODEL 
25 
Figure 5-3: Switching Losses 
 
Figure 5-4: Typical Snubber Circuit 
VSC is equipped with the RC snubbers and series R-L elements to reduce the ЭҖЭ’ЭҖЭҗ
вҒ„
 and 
ЭҖЭ…ЭҖЭҗ
вҒ„

A turn-off snubber is typically composed of Ьҙ and ЬҘ elements, and its function is to 
absorb stored inductive energy of the circuit, caused by the surge voltage ЭҖЭ’ЭҖЭҗ
вҒ„
 as well 
as Э’ at turn-off can be reduced. Turn-on snubber is designed to reduce ЭҖЭ…ЭҖЭҗ
вҒ„
. [11] 
5.1.4 DC Transmission 
The DC system can be in the form of a transmission line, with underground or overhead 
cables. 
5.1.5 DC Capacitors 
The size of the capacitor depends on the required DC voltage level and the acceptable DC 
ripple. The DC voltage should be adequate for the generation of sinusoidal voltages on 
AC side of the converter. 
The energy stored in the capacitor is released during transients that will help to stabilize 
the power flow on the DC transmission system. The DC capacitor size is characterized 
with a time constant Я¬аҜ–аіҸаіҺ. The time constant Я¬аҜ–аіҸаіҺ can be selected to be small to satisfy 
ripple and transient overvoltage requirement on the DC voltage. A relatively small time 
constant allows fast control of active power and reactive power [10]

5.2 VSC Model Description 
In this part the generic VSC model, which is going to be used, according to [12] will be 
described. 
==PAGE:46==
 
Figure 5-5: Hierarchy Structure of Modular Multi-level Voltage Source Converter (MMC-VSC) Control Systems [12] 
In the construction of the generic VSC model, in this thesis, Type 6 Phasor Models of 
[12] is used. Phasor models, also called electro-mechanical models, RMS models, or 
fundamental frequency models, are used in electro-mechanical simulation tools. The 
study of medium-term (time frame 400ms to 10s) and long-term (10s to several min) 
power systems transients can be performed with time-domain or frequency domain 
analysis. [12]

Phasor models are submitted to all inherent limitations of the phasor modeling approach. 
The two assumptions that lie at the base of the quasi-stationary assumption are: [12] 
пӮ· all harmonics are neglected;  
пӮ· a perfectly sinusoidal signal is assumed. 
In addition to the time-domain calculations, the modal analysis is available for small-
signal stability studies. The representation of the network model is equivalent to the 
representation used for the balanced RMS simulation. [12] 
 
Figure 5-6: VDC Simplified Single-Line Diagram 
Regarding the Figure 5-5, the control levels are briefly described below. 
5.2.1 Dispatch Controls  
Station or Dispatch controls are all the controls that manage the operating set points (ЬёаҜ—аҜ–, 
ЬёаҜ”аҜ–, etc.) or the operating control modes for the converter to meet both AC and DC system 
requirements. [12] 
5.2.2 Upper Level Controls  
The upper level accepts P, Q, ЬёаҜ—аҜ–, ЬёаҜ”аҜ– reference orders from the dispatch controls. Within 
the upper level control, configuration is required depending on whether the control is 
connected to an AC system with active synchronous generation (non-islanded system) or 
an islanded AC system with passive loads only or with limited generation. 
5.2.2.1 Non-islanded controls (Grid-Imposed Frequency VSC System [13]) 
Current vector control strategy is based on regulating the direct (d) and quadrature (q) 
components of the AC current. A phase-locked loop generates the reference frame angle 
Я  by locking onto the AC voltage ЬёаҜ”аҜ•аҜ– at the point of common-coupling (PCC) with the 
grid.  
==PAGE:48==
The d and q reference currents Э…аҜ— and Э…аҜӨ are produced by the active and reactive power 
control loops. The active power loop can be configured to control either the DC voltage 
ЬёаҜ—аҜ– or active power P. The reactive power control loop can be selected to regulate either 
the AC voltage, the reactive power Q or the power factor at the PCC. The multiplication 
of measured active power and tan(П•) results in the desired reactive power which fulfills 
the desired power factor. 
The current references Э…аҜ— and Э…аҜӨ are applied to a current limiter block. The outputs of the 
current limiter stage are then given to the decoupled current regulator block. This stage 
produces the reference d and q voltages Э’аҜ— and Э’аҜӨ. 
5.2.2.2 Islanded operation (Controlled-Frequency VSC System [13]) 
The set of controls in this path are used when the HVDC VSC converter is connected to 
an AC system with disconnected load or with asynchronous generation. It can also be 
used when connecting to very weak AC systems containing synchronous generation 
where it is desired for the converter to have an active role in the AC system frequency 
control. [12] 
From the functional point of view, one of the main differences between this control path 
and the non-islanded control path is the origin of the angle reference. In the non-islanded 
control path, the angle reference comes from the phase locked loop (PLL), whereas in the 
islanded operation the angle reference is generated by an independent oscillator 
controlling the system frequency. [12] 
5.2.3 Lower Level Controls 
The lower level controls are responsible for the development of firing pulses necessary to 
produce the AC waveforms that were requested by the upper level controls. The lower 
level controls can change widely depending on the type of valve being used: two or three 
levels versus modular multilevel and even other configurations. Different modulation 
techniques may enhance the performance of a converter, when an individual station is 
concerned. [12] 
==PAGE:49==
 
VSC TECHNOLOGY & GENERIC VSC MODEL 
29 
5.2.4 Upper Level Control Configuration вҖ“ Current Vector Control 
 
Figure 5-7: Current-Controlled Real-/Reactive-Power Controller in dq-Frame 
Two main methods exist for controlling ЬІаҜҰ and ЬіаҜҰ in the VSC system. The п¬Ғrst approach, 
known as voltage vector (voltage-mode) control, has been dominantly utilized in high-
voltage/-power applications such as in FACTS controllers. The voltage vector control is 
simple and has a low number of control loops. However, the main shortcoming of the 
voltage-mode control is that there is no control loop closed on the VSC line current. [13] 
The second approach to the control of ЬІаҜҰ and ЬіаҜҰ in the VSC system is referred to as the 
current vector (current-mode) control. In this approach, the VSC line current is tightly 
regulated by a dedicated current-control scheme, through the VSC AC-side terminal 
voltage. Then, ЬІаҜҰ and ЬіаҜҰ are controlled by the phase angle and the amplitude of the VSC 
line current with respect to the PCC voltage. Thus, due to the current regulation scheme, 
the VSC is protected against overcurrent conditions. [13]

Figure 5-8:VSC Control System 
Current vector control is developed in two control levels, the lower level control (inner 
loop) and the upper level control (outer loop). [14] 
5.2.4.1 Inner Loop 
The control structure is formed by proportional-integral controller (PI) that regulates the 
current through inductor. There are decoupling terms to allow independent d-axis and q-
axis current control. [14] 
5.2.4.2 Outer Loop 
The outer loop calculates the current reference to obtain the desired operational sets 
related with active and reactive power output of converter. [14] 
5.2.4.3 Phase-locked Loop - PLL 
The PLL is required to extract the angle needed to synchronize the control system. [14]

5.2.5 Dynamic Model in Frequency Domain 
There are two options in DigSilent PowerFactory for conducting simulations: a) RMS 
Simulation and b) EMT Simulation.  
In RMS Simulation, frequency domain equations for the electrical network are being used 
- steady-state representation of the passive electrical network; differential equations are 
only for the mechanic transients (e.g. Swing equation) [15] [16]  
In EMT Simulation, voltages and currents are represented by their instantaneous values, 
so that the dynamic behavior of passive network elements is considered. [15] 
Since in following simulations are done with DigSilentвҖҷs RMS Simulation, the generic 
model of VSC has to be built for frequency domain. Therefore, at the beginning it is 
needed to introduce equations and related parameters in frequency domain, because 
вҖңEach solution is valid in its domainвҖқ [17] .

Э’МҒаҜҡаҜ—(Эҗ) sin ЯұаҜ—аҜӨЭҗ+ Э’МҒаҜҡаҜӨ(Эҗ) cos ЯұаҜ—аҜӨЭҗвҲ’Э’МҒаҜ аҜ—(Эҗ) sin ЯұаҜ—аҜӨЭҗвҲ’Э’МҒаҜ аҜӨ(Эҗ) cos ЯұаҜ—аҜӨЭҗ

5.2.5.2 Phase-Locked Loop 
A phase-locked loop is a circuit that synchronizes the signal from an oscillator with a 
second input signal, called the reference, so that they operate at the same frequency. The 
synchronized oscillator is commonly a voltage-controlled oscillator (VCO). [18] 
5.2.5.2.1 Basic Equations of PLL 
 
Figure 5-11: Basic Feedback Network of PLL 
Each PLL system is composed of four basic parts: [19] 
1. the reference generator (RG) 
2. the phase detector (PD) 
3. the low-pass п¬Ғlter Fаӯҗ(f) (in higher-order systems) 
4. the voltage-controlled oscillator (VCO) 
The input signal by RG: 
Э’аҜң(Эҗ) = ЬёаҜңsin[ЯұаҜңЭҗ+ Я¶аҜң(Эҗ)] = ЬёаҜңsin ОЁаҜң(Эҗ) 
(5-47) 
 
The output signal at VCO: 
Э’аҜў(Эҗ) = ЬёаҜўsin[ЯұаҜўЭҗ+ Я¶аҜў(Эҗ)] = ЬёаҜўsin ОЁаҜў(Эҗ) 
(5-48) 
 
PD Signal: 
Э’аҜ—(Эҗ) = ЬӯаҜ Э’аҜң(Эҗ)Э’аҜў(Эҗ) 
(5-49) 
 
Э’аҜ—(Эҗ) = ЬӯаҜ ЬёаҜңЬёаҜўsin ОЁаҜң(Эҗ) cos ОЁаҜў(Эҗ)
= 1
2 ЬӯаҜ ЬёаҜңЬёаҜўаө«sinаө«(ЯұаҜңвҲ’ЯұаҜў)Эҗ+ Я¶аҜң(Эҗ) вҲ’Я¶аҜў(Эҗ)аөҜ
+ sinаө«(ЯұаҜң+ ЯұаҜў)Эҗ+ Я¶аҜң(Эҗ) + Я¶аҜў(Эҗ)аөҜаөҜ 
(5-50) 
 
ЬӯаҜ—= ЬӯаҜ ЬёаҜңЬёаҜў
(5-51) 
 
The signal after the low-pass filter: 
Э’а¬¶(Эҗ) = ЬӯаҜ—sinаө«(ЯұаҜңвҲ’ЯұаҜў)Эҗ+ Я¶аҜң(Эҗ) вҲ’Я¶аҜў(Эҗ)аөҜ= ЬӯаҜ—sin ОЁаҜҳ(Эҗ) 
(5-52) 
 
The phase error: 
ОЁаҜҳ(Эҗ) = ОЁаҜң(Эҗ) вҲ’ОЁаҜў(Эҗ) 
(5-53)

VSC MODEL in DIGSILENT 
The model equations for the two-level converter are derived from the circuit according to 
Figure 6-1. The circuit is composed of valves with turn-off capability (two dashes), which 
are usually realized by IGBTs. However, fundamental frequency models for Load Flow, 
Stability etc. are valid for other circuit designs as well, e.g. three level designs. Only the 
detailed PWM-converter model for EMT-simulations is restricted to the topology 
according to Figure 6-1. [20] 
 
Figure 6-1: Equivalent Circuit, with DC-capacitance (included in the model only for RMS-simulations [20] 
No-load losses and load losses are included in the model, represented by a resistance 
between the DC terminals and a series resistance in AC grid respectively. A series 
reactance is also included to simplify the modelling. However, the DC capacitor is not 
included, so it has to be added externally. [21] 
 
Figure 6-2: PWM-converter with no-load losses, AC grid side reactance and load-losses [20] 
PWM converter losses are specified in model as: [20] 
пӮ· No-load losses: specified with the parameter Pnold in [kW] 
==PAGE:62==
пӮ· Switching losses: specified with the parameter swtLossFactor in [kW/A] 
пӮ· Resistive losses: specified with the parameter resLossFactor in [О©] 
6.1 Composite Frame and Models (Types for VSC Model) 
Before defining controller elements (composite model and common models), DigSilent 
requires definitions of composite frame and models for those like type of an element. In 
this section both graphical expressions and equations related with those types are going 
to be represented. 
Equations related with initialization are important for a smooth start to simulation; even 
given initial values for inputs and/or outputs are enough to start model definition, they 
might not be proper in a composite frame after a load flow solution. Therefore, it is also 
critical for smooth start selecting built-in models to use, which may not in harmony with 
the composite frame and load flow data coming to the composite frame. For example, 
built-in вҖңdq-ir TransformationвҖқ couldnвҖҷt be used in the model.

6.1.2.3.1 User Defined Macro: Limiting_q: 
i_mag_1=lim(sqrt(sqr(iq)+sqr(id)),0,i_max_1) 
id_lim_1=lim(id,-i_max_1,i_max_1) 
iq_lim_1=iq/max(abs(iq),1.0e-09)*sqrt(max(sqr(i_mag_1)-sqr(id_lim_1),0)) 
6.1.2.3.2 User Defined Macro: Limiting_both: 
i_mag_2=lim(sqrt(sqr(id)+sqr(iq)),0,i_max_2) 
id_lim_2=i_mag_2/max(sqrt(sqr(id)+sqr(iq)),1.0e-9)*id 
iq_lim_2=i_mag_2/max(sqrt(sqr(id)+sqr(iq)),1.0e-9)*iq 
6.1.2.3.3 User Defined Macro: Limiting_d: 
i_mag_3=lim(sqrt(sqr(id)+sqr(iq)),0,i_max_3) 
iq_lim_3=lim(iq,-i_max_3,i_max_3) 
id_lim_3=id/max(abs(id),1.0e-09)*sqrt(max(sqr(i_mag_3)-sqr(iq_lim_3),0))

6.1.2.5.5 Fault Ride Through 
 
Figure 6-14: Fault Ride Through - FRT 
6.1.2.5.5.1 User Defined Macro: keep_min 
float=select(abs(i2)< abs(o1),i2, o1) 
o1=select(picdro_const(i1,0,1),float,i2) 
6.1.2.5.5.2 User Defined Macro: ramping 
t=time() 
inc(flt)=0 
inc(p_cleared)=0 
yllw=select(time()-t_clear=0.or.time()-t_clear>1,yellow,0) 
flt=flipflop(yllw,flt) 
t_clear=aflipflop(time(),flt,yllw) 
p_cleared=aflipflop(p_clear,flt,yllw) 
p_ramp=lim(p_cleared+((t-t_clear)/Tn)*(p_set/abs(p_set)),-abs(p_set),abs(p_set)) 
6.1.2.5.5.3 User Defined Macro: 3_selector 
inc(y1)=x1 
inc(status)=0 
status=flipflop(a2,abs(x1-x4)<0.00001) 
y1=select(a1=1,0,select(a2=1,select(delay(a1,0.02)=1,0,x2),select(a2=1,x2,select(status
=0,x1, x3))))

a. Input Signals: 
Pmd: Pulse-width modulation index, d-axis [20]

cosref: cos of reference angle [20] 
sinref: sin of reference angle [20] 
This set of input variables is convenient in grid-connected applications. It allows 
specifying a pulse-width modulation index-vector, with reference to a reference-system 
that is deп¬Ғned by ЬҝЭӢЭҸЭҺЭҒЭӮ and ЭҸЭ…ЭҠЭҺЭҒЭӮ. [20]

6.2.2 PWM#n_Mode Control_P 
a) Operational Parameter (Set): 
With the parameter вҖңSetвҖқ, which control mode for active power control will be used, can 
be selected. вҖң0вҖқ denotes вҖңConstant Active PowerвҖқ control mode, вҖң1вҖқ denotes вҖңConstant 
DC VoltageвҖқ control mode, вҖң2вҖқ denotes вҖңFrequency Sensitivity ModeвҖқ control mode and 
вҖң3вҖқ denotes вҖңSynthetic InertiaвҖқ control mode. 
6.2.3 PWM#n_Mode Control_Q 
a) Operational Parameter (Set): 
With the parameter вҖңSetвҖқ, which control mode for reactive power control will be used, 
can be selected. вҖң0вҖқ denotes вҖңConstant Reactive PowerвҖқ control mode, вҖң1вҖқ denotes вҖңAC 
Voltage DroopвҖқ control mode, вҖң2вҖқ denotes вҖңConstant Power FactorвҖқ control mode.

вҖңwLвҖқ is the inductance value of PWM converter in p.u.

6.2.5 PWM#n_Current Limiter 
a) PWM Parameter (i_max_1, i_max_2, i_max_3): 
вҖқi_max_1вҖқ is the maximum current magnitude in p.u. in case of the first priority at Э…аҜ—. 
вҖқi_max_2вҖқ is the maximum current magnitude in p.u. in case there isnвҖҷt any priority 
between Э…аҜ— and Э…аҜӨ. 
вҖқi_max_3вҖқ is the maximum current magnitude in p.u. in case of the first priority at Э…аҜӨ. 
b) Operational Parameter (V_red, V_yellow): 
==PAGE:79==
 
VSC MODEL in DIGSILENT

Priority by default at Э…аҜ—, and itвҖҷs shifting according to p.u. voltage magnitude at PWMвҖҷs

Figure 6-29: Description of Synthetic Inertia ModeвҖҷs Parameters 
вҖқmdвҖқ parameter is used to implement an operational measure, which is not possible for 
inertia response of conventional -/a-synchronous machine. For example, in case of a 
frequency droop, conventional machine is transforming its stored kinetical energy to 
electrical energy and starts recover it right after an increase in frequency, even the 
frequency level is below the nominal value. 
With вҖңmdвҖқ parameter, if itвҖҷs selected as вҖң0вҖқ, operation in Zone-2 and Zone-3 are 
prohibited; it means, contrary to response of conventional machine, PWM converter 
wonвҖҷt start recovering energy until the frequency reaches its nominal value after 
disturbance. 
If same operation with conventional machine is required, вҖңmdвҖқ can simply be chosen as 
вҖң-1вҖқ.

6.2.7.4 Const_P

6.2.7.5 FRT-P 
a) Operational Parameter (U_block, U_fault, Tn): 
вҖңU_blockвҖқ is the blocking voltage level in p.u. to protect PWM in case of fault in the 
system. 
вҖңU_faultвҖқ is the voltage level in p.u. taken as limit, which indicates a fault in the system. 
вҖңTnвҖқ is the post fault recovery time duration to reach nominal power at active power. 
(see. Figure 6-30)

The design parameters of the loop filter are the damping ratio ЯҰ and the natural frequency 
ЯұаҜЎ. The damping ratio can be chosen by the Wiener method аө«ЯҰ= вҲҡ2 2
вҒ„ аөҜ. The bandwidth 
of the loop filter is a trade-off between the filtering characteristics and fast responses. 
While the higher bandwidth ensures the faster dynamic responses, the tracking error is 
increased under distorted utility conditions, which are phase unbalancing, voltage 
harmonics and voltage offset. [27] 
As stated before in RMS simulations done with DigSilent, it is assumed that the utility is 
in undistorted condition.

6.3 Measurement Elements (StaVmea, StaImea) 
6.3.1 PWM#n DC Current (StaImea) 
No.of Phases = 3 
Measurement Point = PWM#nвҖҷs cubicle at related Terminal/Busbar 
Current Rating = Rating of Connected Element 
6.3.2 PWM#n AC Voltage (StaVmea) 
No.of Phases = 3 
Measurement Point = PWM#nвҖҷs cubicle at related Terminal/Busbar 
Voltage Rating = Rating of Connected Element 
Frequency Output = calculate only if signal is connected

COMPARISON GENERIC MODEL with PUBLISHED RESULTS 
69 
7 
COMPARISON GENERIC MODEL with 
PUBLISHED RESULTS 
In this chapter, the previously explained VSC HVDC Controller Model is going to be 
compared with the results of a published paper via simulating its cases to verify the model. 
The mentioned paper is given at the reference [28]. 
7.1 Grid Description 
The test is going to be described. First the test grid topology with a single-line diagram 
and grid elementsвҖҷ general specifications is being introduced and then grid elementsвҖҷ 
parameter is being given in detail. 
7.1.1 Grid Topology 
Monopolar HVDC link is used in the test grid, left-hand is Master side, where Constant 
DC Voltage mode as active power control and Constant Reactive Power mode as reactive 
power control are enabled; and right-hand is Slave side, where Constant Active Power 
mode as active power control and Droop AC Voltage mode as reactive power control are 
enabled.  
At DC grid, between Master and Slave PWM there is a DC Line. Both Master and Slave 
PWM have their own DC Capacitor groups.  
At Master AC Side, Master PWM is connected to an ideal AC Source via a Grid 
Reactance. And at Slave AC Side, where investigation will take place, Slave PWM is 
connected to an ideal AC Source via two parallel reactance, one large and one small size 
as a changing representation SCR of the grid at PCC with Slave PWM. Small-reactance 
is divided to section with same size to implement fault in the middle of the line, which is 
one of cases. Last AC side reactance and resistance of both Master and Slave PWMs are 
defined within their PWM elements. 
==PAGE:90==
 
Figure 7-1: Single Line Diagram of the Grid used in Simulated Cases 
7.1.2 Grid Elements 
In this part, parameters of elements, which are required for DigSilent RMS Simulation, 
are given. 
7.1.2.1 AC Sources 
Both AC Sources are ideal sources, the voltage set point is 1ЭҢ. Э‘. at their own terminals. 
7.1.2.2 VSCs 
Basic Data of both PWMs: The converter type for PWMs is Two-level Converter and 
their modulation type is Sinusoidal PWM. Rated AC and DC voltages of VSCs are 40ЭҮЬё 
and 80ЭҮЬё respectively and rated power of them is 100ЬҜЬ№. PWMвҖҷs Series ReactorвҖҷs 
Short Circuit Impedance is 20% and Series ReactorвҖҷs Copper Losses is 1000ЭҮЬ№. 
Load Flow of Master PWM: The Control Mode is вҖңVdc-QвҖқ, the set point of DC Voltage 
is 1ЭҢ. Э‘. and controlled node is the DC terminal of Master PWM. Reactive Power set point 
is 0ЬҜЬёЬЈЭҺ. 
Load Flow of Slave PWM: The Control Mode is вҖңP-VacвҖқ, the set point of AC Voltage is 
1ЭҢ. Э‘. at the AC terminal of Slave PWM, and active power set point is varying during 
simulations.  
RMS Simulation of both PWMs: There isnвҖҷt any VSC losses defined. VSC No-Load 
Losses = 0ЭҮЬ№, VSC Switching Loss Factor = 0 ЭҮЬ№ЬЈ
вҒ„  and VSC Resistive Loss Factor = 
0О©. 
7.1.2.3 Terminals 
Rated voltage of AC and DC Terminals are 40ЭҮЬё and 80ЭҮЬё, respectively.

7.1.2.4 Reactors 
There are 3 different reactors are used in the system to describe the strength of AC grids. 
All their Rated Voltage and Rated Power are equal to 40ЭҮЬё and 100ЬҜЬёЬЈ, respectively. 
The Grid ReactanceвҖҷs Short-Circuit uk is equal 6%, LX (large reactance) 200%, and last 
SX-1 and SX-2 (small reactance is split two parts) 5%. 
7.1.2.5 Lines 
There is only a DC Line, its Rated Current is 10ЭҮЬЈ, Positive Sequence Resistance (R1) 
is 0.4О© and last Positive Sequence Reactance (X1) is 0.6283185О©. 
7.1.2.6 Capacitors 
DC Capacitor rating of Master and Slave PWMs are Nominal Voltage = 80ЭҮЬё, Rated 
Reactive Power (Cap) = 80ЬҜЬёЬЈЭҺ, Loss Factor (ЭҗЬҪЭҠЯң) = 0, Susceptance = 37500 ЯӨЬө.

when the AC terminal voltage drops between 0.9ЭҢ. Э‘. and 0.85ЭҢ. Э‘., there isnвҖҷt any 
priority between reference currents, and last when the AC terminal voltage drops further 
than 0.85, q-axis current reference (Ь«аҜӨ_аҜҘаҜҳаҜҷ) takes the priority. Accordingly, V_red and

7.2 Case Description 
The subject of the referred paper is to investigate the system response to a sudden large 
drop of the SCR, which illustrates, that a previously strong grid is suddenly weakening 
due to two main events. [28] 
The analyzation way of the paper is taken as a reference for analyses; so, analyses are 
done in 3 parts. 
7.2.1 Small Signal Stability 
In the first analysis is done for finding the small disturbance stability limit, in case there 
is only LX in operation. The model analysis tool of DigSilent is used for this purpose, the 
selected calculation method is вҖңQR/QZ-Method_QR Method using system reductionвҖқ. 
7.2.2 Short-Circuit 
In the second and third analyses, large disturbance stability limits are investigated. For 
those analyses, the first case is a short-circuit event in the middle of the SX (between SX-
1 and SX-2). Short-circuit is occurring at 0.1ЭҸ and lasting for 100ЭүЭҸ and clearing with 
circuit breaker operations at each edge. If the terminal voltage drops down below 0.2ЭҢ. Э‘., 
Slave_PWM is going to block its transactions but stay connected to the grid; after fault 
clearing the Slave_PWM is ramping up, which defined at Sections 6.1.2.5.5 and 6.2.7.5, 
back to its pre-disturbance value. 
Short-Circuit event analyses are done with RMS Simulation of DigSilent, the Integration 
Step Size is chosen as 0.25ЭүЭҸ for Electromechanical Transients and the duration is 5ЭҸ.  
Three simulation results, which are referring 3 different loading condition of the 
Slave_PWM, for this event are shared in the result part. The first loading condition is 
referring the large disturbance stability limit of the system (46.2ЬҜЬ№), the second is the 
small disturbance stability limit (47.5ЬҜЬ№), the result of the first part, and the last 
impossible transferring situation in case of only LX in operation (80ЬҜЬ№), whose value 
taken from [28]. 
7.2.3 Line Opening вҖ“ Maneuver 
The second case, in large disturbance analyses, is investigating large disturbance stability, 
in case there is a wrong maneuver вҖ“ mis-operation вҖ“ in the system, which makes SX (both 
SX-1 and SX-2) opened at two ends. The maneuver occurs at 0.1ЭҸ by opening of edge 
circuit breakers of SX. 
==PAGE:96==
Line Opening event analyses are done with RMS Simulation of DigSilent, the Integration 
Step Size is chosen as 0.25ЭүЭҸ for Electromechanical Transients and the duration is 1ЭҸ.  
Three simulation results, which are referring 3 different loading condition of the 
Slave_PWM, for this event are shared in the result part. The first loading condition is 
referring the large disturbance stability limit of the system (36.3ЬҜЬ№), the second is the 
large disturbance stability limit (37ЬҜЬ№) calculated in the referred paper [28], and the last 
the stability limit in the Short-Circuit event (46.2ЬҜЬ№). 
7.3 Results of Analyses 
7.3.1 Small Signal Stability Analysis 
Before investigating a stable operational point in case of losing flow over SX, it is more 
adequate to find out first a stable operational point in case of small disturbance, where 
SX isnвҖҷt in operation. This operational point is going to be used as a reference point for 
large disturbance analyses. 
The stable operational limit is found at 47.5ЬҜЬ№ active power set-point of Slave_PWM. 
In the Figure 7-3, it is given the grid structure with the load-flow solution at small-
disturbance/signal stability limit. 
 
Figure 7-3: Grid for Small-Signal Analysis with Load-Flow Solution at Stability Limit 
7.3.2 Short-Circuit 
Terminal Voltage, Active-Reactive Powers, PLL Angle and Frequency outputs of the 
Slave_PWM will be represented for three set-points, explained in the Section 7.2.2. The 
large disturbance stability limit (46.2ЬҜЬ№) is close to small-signal stability limit 
(47ЬҜЬ№), as probably expected result after a fault, but the main reason behind that 
gradually ramping up of active power after fault clearing and reaching its set-point in a 
definite time, which can be seen at the Figure 7-6.

7.3.3 Line Opening вҖ“ Maneuver 
Terminal Voltage, Active-Reactive Powers, PLL Angle and Frequency outputs of the 
Slave_PWM will be represented for three set-points, explained in the Section 7.2.2. The 
first set-point is the stability limit for wrong maneuver incident, the second set-point is 
the stability limit given in the paper [28] and the last set-point is the stability limit for 
short-circuit incident. 
The difference between stability limits of two incidents, short-circuit and wrong 
maneuver, can be caused by, that the active power is ramping up after fault-clearing, on 
the other hand there isnвҖҷt any ramping up after circuit breaker opening, because the 
voltage doesnвҖҷt drop below the level, which introduces to the converter, there is a fault in 
the power system.

Figure 7-11: Case 2 вҖ“ Slave_PWM Terminal Voltage 
After breaker opening, beyond transient on the terminal voltage magnitude, its phase 
angle is considerably differing due to huge increase, around 20 times, on equivalent 
reactance and pre-maneuver power set points of the converter. Although active power 
output of the converter has decreased immediately due to drop of the d-axis terminal 
voltage (ЬёаҜҡаҜ—), caused by the phase difference, active power output of the converter starts 
transiently increasing due to rapid response of Outer Loop (Ь«аҜ—_аҜҘаҜҳаҜҷ) compared to PLLвҖҷs.  
Until PLL, for which ЯҷаҜЈаҜҹаҜҹвү…28.28ЬӘЭ– (Ь¶аҜЈаҜҹаҜҹвү…0.035ЭҸ) is defined, reacts and starts to fix

GRID RECOMMENDATION for SIMULATION with SYNCHRONOUS GENERATORS 
85 
8 
GRID RECOMMENDATION for SIMULATION 
with SYNCHRONOUS GENERATORS 
8.1 Grid Description 
This chapter is introducing an alternative grid to the analyzed grid in Chapter 7. There are 
two main changes compared to the grid given in the Figure 7-1. First, synchronous 
generators are used instead of ideal voltage sources; second change on the representation 
of physical weakening grid. 
The subject of this work, as well as building a generic controller model, is to analyze 
VSC-HVDCвҖҷs support mechanism to futureвҖҷs girds. In future grids, not only there will be 
a great share of static sources in power generation, which make grids weaker; but also, 
this share will fluctuate time to time, i.e. grids alternate being from strong to weak 
depending on generation mix. 
The reason behind the weakening in [28] is not satisfy to effect of static sources, itвҖҷs 
probably due to using ideal source. It represents more a classical transient problem, where 
a VSC-HVDC is connected to the rest of the grid with highly asymmetrically parallel 
transmission lines and the line, with less impedance value, is failing for some reasons; 
than a problem, caused by unplanned changes on rotational sources (any kind of 
synchronous generators), which make the grid weak, in terms of low SCR. 
It would like to be analyzed the reaction of VSC-HVDC unit to failing of rotational 
sources due to short-circuit and mis-operation, which suddenly makes the grid faced with 
weak grid conditions, low SCR. Changing ideal sources with synchronous generators 
allows to express an alternative grid, which may a way of representation of a physical 
grid, losing high portion of its rotational sources. 
8.1.1 Grid Topology 
Compared to the grid in the Figure 7-1, ideal voltage sources and reactance are replaced 
with synchronous generator, transformers and load. The connection topology is also 
revised; as seen in the Figure 8-1, at Slave_PWM side, the grid has a common coupling, 
where Slave_PWM, a load and two different size synchronous generators and 
transformers groups are connected.  
==PAGE:106==
Conventional generator (Conv_Gen) is operating as a synchronous compensator to 
support the grid in terms of inertia and short-circuit capacity. Small generation 
(Small_Gen) is symbolizing a rotational but small renewable generation, like geothermal 
or waste power plant. Last the load is used for description of local consumption or power 
transfer over LLC based DC system. 
The SCR of the grid in the Chapter 7 is 10.5, when two reactors in parallel, and 0.5, when 
there is only the large reactance left. So, nominal powers of Small_Gen and Conv_Gen 
are selected to satisfy these SCRs. 
In terms of stored kinetic energy in the grid (Ь§аҜһ,аҜҰаҜ¬аҜҰ) and effective DC inertia constant 
(ЬӘаҜ—аҜ–), according to Equations (4-1) and (2-3), the grid at Slave_PWM has Ь§аҜһ,аҜҰаҜ¬аҜҰ=
16.82ЭҢ. Э‘. ЭҸ and ЬӘаҜ—аҜ–= 16.82ЭҸ Small_Gen together with Conv_Gen; and only with 
Small_Gen Ь§аҜһ,аҜҰаҜ¬аҜҰ= 0.82ЭҢ. Э‘. ЭҸ and ЬӘаҜ—аҜ–= 0.82ЭҸ 
 
Figure 8-1: Single Line Diagram of the Alternative Grid with Synchronous Generators 
8.1.2 Grid Elements 
In this part, parameters of elements, which are required for DigSilent RMS Simulation 
and different or new than Section 7.1.2, are given. 
8.1.2.1 Synchronous Generators 
3 synchronous generators are used: they all have same Nominal Voltages = 21ЭҮЬё and 
Power Factor = 0.95; Conv_Gen and Mast_Gen are same size (500ЬҜЬёЬЈ) and Small_Gen 
is much smaller (25.625ЬҜЬёЬЈ) to satisfy SCRs; however, except sizes, per unit 
parameters of generators are same and taken from [32].  
Inertia Constant вҖңHвҖқ, rated to Sgn, is equal to 4. StatorвҖҷs Resistance вҖңrstrвҖқ and Leakage 
Reactance вҖңxlвҖқ are 0 ЭҢ. Э‘. and 0.15 ЭҢ. Э‘., respectively.

8.1.2.2 VSCs 
There isnвҖҷt much change on converters. Differences about their Rated AC (400ЭҮЬё) and 
DC voltages 800ЭҮЬё, Rated Powers (125ЬҜЬ№) and Series ReactorвҖҷs Copper Losses 
(1250ЭҮЬ№). Changes are done because of usage of generator & transformer couples and 
needs to satisfy the SCR. 
8.1.2.3 Terminals 
Rated voltages of AC terminals are 21ЭҮЬё at MV level and 400ЭҮЬё at HV level; rated 
voltage of DC terminal is 800ЭҮЬё. 
8.1.2.4 Lines 
The DC Line type parameters are taken from [12]. Its Rated Current is 2.265ЭҮЬЈ, Positive 
Sequence Resistance (R1) is 1.1О© and Positive Sequence Reactance (X1) is 
0.00164305О© for 100ЭҮЭү long line. 
8.1.2.5 Capacitors 
DC Capacitor rating of Master and Slave PWMs are Nominal Voltage = 800ЭҮЬё, Rated 
Reactive Power (Cap) = 100ЬҜЬёЬЈЭҺ, Loss Factor (ЭҗЬҪЭҠЯң) = 0, Susceptance = 468.75 ЯӨЬө. 
8.1.2.6 Transformers 
Three transformers are used to connect generators to the grid, their parameters are taken 
from [32]. All of them have rated voltages (HV: 400ЭҮЬё) & (LV: 21ЭҮЬё), Short-Circuit 
Voltage (uk: 16%) and SHC-Voltage (Re(uk)), (ukr: 0.15%). 
Only their rated powers are different, C-Trafo and M-Trafo have 500ЬҜЬёЬЈ and R-Trafo 
has 25.625ЬҜЬёЬЈ.

8.1.2.8 Station Control 
For managing a smooth start to simulation, itвҖҷs necessary to mimic control philosophy of 
RMS-Simulation in load flow calculation. Because there isnвҖҷt a default AC voltage droop 
control for VSC, a station control unit is defined for this purpose. 
The station control is controlling the common busbarвҖҷs voltage by setting it to 1ЭҢ. Э‘. with 
a distribution of duty according to nominal powers of Conv_Gen (80%) and Slave_PWM 
(20%).

8.1.2.9.1 Slave PWM

7.1.2.7.1 are used. 
8.1.2.9.2 Master PWM 
Since there isnвҖҷt any change in per unit level, same controller parameters with the Section 
7.1.2.7.2 are used.

8.2 Case Description 
Simulations described here have similar aim with done in the Chapter 7, it is to investigate 
the system response to a sudden large drop of the SCR, but this time the reason is losing 
rotating sources. Conv_Gen is operated as synchronous condenser (ЬІаҜўаҜЁаҜ§= 0 & ЬёаҜүа®ја®ј=
1 ЭҢ. Э‘.), and Small_Gen is controlling voltage only on its own-bus, there isnвҖҷt any duty to 
support transmission system voltage for it. 
8.2.1 Small Signal Stability 
The first analysis is done for finding the small disturbance stability limit, in case there is 
only Small_Gen in operation. The model analysis tool of DigSilent is used for this 
purpose, the selected calculation method is вҖңQR/QZ-Method_QR Method using system 
reductionвҖқ. 
8.2.2 Short-Circuit 
Stability limits for in the light of two variables are investigated. First, different active 
power generation levels of Small_Gen, and second different reactive power demand 
(compensation level) of the load. 
==PAGE:111==
 
GRID RECOMMENDATION for SIMULATION with SYNCHRONOUS GENERATORS 
91 
The levels of Small_Gen generation and LoadвҖҷs PF can be seen at the Table 8-6. The base 
scenario is Load has 0.707 PF and Small_Gen has 51% generation level, which is called 
as в‘ . Numbers In cells next to scenario numbering are corresponding the active power 
transfer of the converter and the ratio to its nominal power. The active power of the load 
is corresponding to summation of active powers of the converter and Small_Gen. 
The event, which is causing the loss of Conv_Gen, is Short-Circuit on its own terminal at 
the time Эҗ= 1ЭҸ and cleared after 100ЭүЭҸ by opening of breakers. Short-Circuit event 
analyses are done with RMS Simulation of DigSilent, the Integration Step Size is chosen 
as 0.25ЭүЭҸ for Electromechanical Transients and the duration is considerably longer 60ЭҸ, 
because of dynamic response of synchronous generator.

8.2.3 Line Opening вҖ“ Maneuver 
Stability limits for in the light of two variables are investigated. First, different active 
power generation levels of Small_Gen, and second different reactive power demand 
(compensation level) of the load. 
The levels of Small_Gen generation (according to ЬөаҜЎаҜўаҜ ) and LoadвҖҷs PF can be seen at 
the Table 8-7.The base scenario is Load has 0.707 PF and Small_Gen has 51% generation 
level, which is called as в‘ . Values, in cells next to scenario numbering, are corresponding 
the active power transfer of the converter and the ratio to its nominal power. The active 
power of the load is corresponding to summation of active powers of the converter and 
Small_Gen. 
The event, which is causing the loss of Conv_Gen, is opening of its breaker at the time 
Эҗ= 1ЭҸ. Short-Circuit event analyses are done with RMS Simulation of DigSilent, the 
Integration Step Size is chosen as 0.25ЭүЭҸ (0.10ЭүЭҸ, for scenarios в‘ў and в‘Ў) for 
Electromechanical Transients and the duration is considerably longer 60ЭҸ, because of 
dynamic response of synchronous generator.

8.3 Results of Simulations 
8.3.1 Small Signal Stability 
The Small Signal stability limit is ЬІаҜҹаҜўаҜ”аҜ—= 103ЬҜЬ№ and ЬіаҜҹаҜўаҜ”аҜ—= 103ЬҜЬёЬЈЭҺ, where 
ЬІаҜҢаҜҹаҜ”аҜ©аҜҳ_аҜүаҜҗаҜҶ= 90ЬҜЬ№ (72% loaded) and ЬІаҜҢаҜ аҜ”аҜҹаҜҹ_аҜҖаҜҳаҜЎ= 13ЬҜЬ№ (51% loaded). 
 
Figure 8-2: Power Flow for Small Signal Stability 
8.3.2 Short-Circuit 
As mentioned in 8.2.2, five scenarios are simulated, where Reactive Power demand 
(compensation level) of the Load and Active Power generation of Small_Gen are main 
variables. Some graphics are represented for comparison effects of mentioned variables. 
Scenario-1 is base for both variations.  
==PAGE:113==
 
GRID RECOMMENDATION for SIMULATION with SYNCHRONOUS GENERATORS 
93 
 
Figure 8-3: Base Scenario (1) power flow 58.9s after Short-Circuit Clearing 
After the fault, the grid at Slave_PWM side comes to islanded conditions for HVDC links, 
as described in [2]. Although integral control for voltage and frequency is required by 
HVDC side to recover nominal values, here, survival of the grid is being investigated at 
constant Active Power and droop Voltage control by Slave_PWM. 
At  Figure 8-4 and Figure 8-5, voltages at PCC and Reactive Power response of 
Slave_PWM with varying Reactive Power demand (compensation level) of the load are 
being showed. The red lines indicate Scenario-1, green lines Scenario-2 and blue 
Scenario-3.  
As seen there are high oscillation both on voltage and reactive power output especially at 
Scenario-2 and Scenario-3, because the steady-state voltage level of Scenario-2 and 
Scenario-3 are very close to 1ЭҢ. Э‘., 0.999ЭҢ. Э‘. and 1.016ЭҢ. Э‘. respectively, so they 
produce fluctuation on droop control (there are different slopes for overvoltage and 
undervoltage scheme, see. 7.1.2.7.1.3). The stability level for Scenario-2 and Scenario-3 
is limited due to this fluctuation, convergence couldnвҖҷt be satisfied for higher power 
demands of the load.

Figure 8-5: Reactive Power of Slave_PWM Scenario 1-2-3

Slave_PWM with varying Active Power generation of Small_Gen are being showed. The 
red lines indicate Scenario-1, green lines Scenario-4 and blue Scenario-5.  
Figure 8-6: Voltage at PCC Scenario 1-4-5 
Figure 8-7: Reactive Power of Slave_PWM Scenario 1-4-5

seen.

simulation of Scenario-2 and Scenario-3, integration step size was decreased to 0.10ЭүЭҸ.)

8.3.4 Comparison with a Little Stronger Grid 
In this section a comparison is made between the grid, introduced in the Section 8.1.1, 
and a stronger but still weak grid, according to [2]. The stronger grid has SCR equal to 
11.37 before incident and 1.6 after incident and ЬӘаҜ—аҜ– equal to 18.176ЭҸ before and 2.176ЭҸ 
after. 
At the Figure 8-21 and Figure 8-22, frequency responses of base scenarios in cases, Short-
Circuit and Maneuver. The green line corresponds to frequency measured by in-built 
Voltage Measurement element and the red line to frequency calculated by PLL block. 
There isnвҖҷt observed an important deviation between them. 
Small_Gen has droop control for frequency (8.1.2.10.3) and Slave_PWM (7.1.2.7.1) has 
constant active power control. As mentioned in the previous sections, due to ramping at 
active power output of Slave_PWM after short-circuit clearing, the system frequency 
drops deepest to 0.870ЭҢ. Э‘. and recovers to 1.009ЭҢ. Э‘. seen at the Figure 8-21; and due to 
decrease of active power output of Small_Gen, while mechanical power output is 
constant, after wrong maneuver, the system frequency increases highest to 1.256ЭҢ. Э‘. at 
the Figure 8-22 and recovers to 1.024ЭҢ. Э‘. at the 300th second.

RESPONSES of VSC UNDER DISTURBANCES in WEAK GRID 
105 
9 
RESPONSES of VSC UNDER DISTURBANCES 
in WEAK GRID 
After investigating survivals of the VSC in the suddenly weakened grid in previous 
chapters, in this chapter VSCвҖҷs contribution to frequency support, fulfilling fault-ride-
through (FRT) requirement, supporting the system in terms of short-circuit currents and 
voltage stabilization capability is going to be investigating in several different events. 
9.1 Grid Description 
As previously introduced grids, there are also 2 isolated AC grids and 1 DC grids. In 
previous chapters, not much information is given about strength of Master_AC grid side, 
all focus was on the Slave_Grid side. Therefore, when itвҖҷs called the grid, it is subjected 
to Slave_Grid. But in this chapter care will be taken about using terminology to prevent 
conflict between grid. 
Before giving more details about grid topologies and used elements, there are some 
figures about strength of two AC grids: Slave_GridвҖҷs SCR and ЬӘаҜ—аҜ– are 1.22 and 2ЭҸ, 
respectively; Master_GridвҖҷs SCR and ЬӘаҜ—аҜ– are 6.1 and 10ЭҸ, respectively; 
9.1.1 Grid Topologies 
The system consists of 2 AC grids and 1 DC grid, separated by monopolar VSC HVDC 
units. 
In the Master_Grid, 2500ЬҜЬёЬЈ Mast_Gen (5 parallel units, each 500ЬҜЬёЬЈ), 2500ЬҜЬёЬЈ 
M-Trafo (5 parallel units, each 500ЬҜЬёЬЈ) and 1000ЬҜЬёЬЈ Master_PWM are serial 
connected. This grid symbolizes a strong grid, which has more conventional power, 
feeding a weaker grid.  
The DC Grid has similar specification with the gird describe in the Section 8.1. There are 
a long DC Line and capacitors at each PWMвҖҷs DC side. 
In the Slave_Grid, there are 3 main unit groups connected to common coupling 
1000ЬҜЬёЬЈ Slave_PWM, 500ЬҜЬёЬЈ Conv_Gen serial connected with 500ЬҜЬёЬЈ C-Trafo 
and a common Load serially connected with a short AC Line, used for separation 
described later. There are also some support elements an additional Load, symbolizing a 
==PAGE:126==
disturbance event, two different size capacitor banks, supporting the system during short-
circuit events. 
 
Figure 9-1: Grid Topologies 
9.1.2 Grid Elements 
9.1.2.1 Synchronous Generators 
For Conv_Gen and Master_Gen, same elements, which based on [32] and described in 
the Section 8.1.2.1, are used. There is only difference at the number of parallel units of 
Master_Gen, it is five. 
9.1.2.2 VSCs 
Changes compared to the Section 8.1.2.2 are both VSCsвҖҷ Rated Powers and Series 
ReactorвҖҷs Copper Losses become 1000ЬҜЬ№ and 2000ЭҮЬ№, respectively. 
9.1.2.3 Terminals 
They are same with the ones, described in the Section 8.1.2.3. 
9.1.2.4 Lines 
DC Line is same with the one, described in the Section 8.1.2.4. 
AC Line type parameters are also taken from [12]. Its Rated Current is 3.555ЭҮЬЈ, Positive 
Sequence Resistance (R1) is 0.01О© and Positive Sequence Reactance (X1) is 
0.1340203О© for 0.5ЭҮЭү long line.  
9.1.2.5 Capacitors 
DC Capacitor rating of Master and Slave PWMs are Nominal Voltage = 800ЭҮЬё, Rated 
Reactive Power (Cap) = 800ЬҜЬёЬЈЭҺ, Loss Factor (ЭҗЬҪЭҠЯң) = 0, Susceptance = 3750 ЯӨЬө.

9.1.2.8 Station Control 
Again, a station control unit is used for smooth start. The station control is controlling the 
common busbarвҖҷs voltage by setting it to 1ЭҢ. Э‘. with a distribution of duty according to 
nominal powers of Conv_Gen (95%) and Slave_PWM (5%).

9.1.2.10 
Synchronous Generator Controllers 
Same controller described in the Section 8.1.2.10 and based on [32] and [33] are used as

For remark, both generator controllers for both voltage and frequency have droop 
characteristic; so, they are not fixing voltage and frequency at their nominal values. While 
Conv_Gen has a line/transformer drop compensation for regulating voltage, itвҖҷs not 
defined for Mast_Gen. [32] 
9.2 Case Description 
9.2.1 Large Disturbance 
In this case, responses of Slave_PWM and system conditions, especially its frequency 
change, against a large disturbance are investigated for different active power control 
mode and settings of Slave_PWM. The large disturbance is defined as a sudden increase 
of active power (150ЬҜЬ№) via connection of the load вҖңP-DisturbanceвҖқ. 
Constant Active Power (0), FSM (2) and Synthetic Inertia (3) are control modes for active 
power, which are going to be investigated. For all control modes nominal active power 
set points is 340ЬҜЬ№.  
As frequency droop in FSM mode, 3%, 6% and 12% are selected; simulations are done 
with and without a 100ЭүЬӘЭ– dead-band, called as FSM in parameter set. The case, with 
frequency droop is equal 6% and without dead-band, is the base case for FSM mode. 
As rate of frequency change droop, called as Hdc in parameter set, in Synthetic Inertia 
mode, 0.25 , 1 and 2 are selected. At the beginning, the base case for Synthetic Inertia 
mode is calculated by the equation (6-40), where quantities taken as ЬҘ= 0.2ЭҢ. Э‘., вҲҶЬ·аҜ—аҜ–=
0.1ЭҢ. Э‘. and вҲҶЭӮ= 0.02ЭҢ. Э‘., according to [8], so itвҖҷs equal to 1. 
Both the Load and P-Disturbance are taken as pure impedance in RMS-simulations.  
For cases, Synthetic Inertia and FSM control mode used, simulation is starting with 
constant power mode and at Эҗ= 20ЭҸ mode is changing and disturbance, connection of P-
Disturbance, is occurring Эҗ= 25ЭҸ and simulations are lasting for 60ЭҸ. The Integration 
Step Size is chosen as 0.25ЭүЭҸ for Electromechanical Transients. 
==PAGE:131==
 
RESPONSES of VSC UNDER DISTURBANCES in WEAK GRID 
111 
9.2.2 Load Rejection 
The base cases for FSM and Synthetic Inertia control mode, specified at the previous 
section 9.2.1, and constant active power are used to investigate PWM_SlaveвҖҷs response 
and the systemвҖҷs condition, especially occurred overvoltage, against rejection 30% of the 
Load. 
The Load is taken as pure impedance in RMS-simulations.  
For cases, Synthetic Inertia and FSM control mode used, simulation is starting with 
constant power mode and at Эҗ= 20ЭҸ mode is changing and load rejection, losing 30% of 
both reactive and active power of the Load, is occurring Эҗ= 25ЭҸ and simulations are 
lasting for 90ЭҸ. The Integration Step Size is chosen as 0.25ЭүЭҸ for Electromechanical 
Transients. 
9.2.3 Short-Circuit 
The aim of short-circuit cases, to testing Fault-Ride-Through capabilities and Short-
Circuit Current contributions of Slave_PWM at different level short-circuit in the system, 
which are represented as specific voltage drops. For the decision of curves/capabilities, 
going to be tested, about FRT and reactive power support during undervoltage, [34], [35] 
and [8] are  used  as references. 
During abnormal voltage condition, below ЬёаҜҷаҜ”аҜЁаҜҹаҜ§, it is considered, that the control modes 
for frequency support (FSM and Synthetic Inertia) is blocked and Constant Active Power 
control mode is the base control mode.  
The Load is taken as pure impedance in RMS-simulations, because it was impossible to 
adjust voltage levels to be investigated except choosing the Load as pure impedance. 
Faults are occurred at the terminal between the Load and the AC Line with adjusted 
inductance values to satisfy required fault voltage level. The AC Line is used for 
separation of fault from common coupling to be able to show Short-Circuit Current or 
Power magnitude. 
Capacitors вҖңSCC Step 1-2-3вҖқ and вҖңSCC Step 1-2вҖқ are used to give support to support 
VSC by fulfilling its reactive power support during undervoltage conditions, shown in 
the Figure 9-2. Instead of two separate capacitors, a controlled 3 -step capacitor bank can 
be used, too, but proper controller has to be introduced. About operation of capacitor 
bank, when the terminal voltage is between 0.7ЭҢ. Э‘. and 0.6ЭҢ. Э‘., only first step connected, 
when between 0.6ЭҢ. Э‘. and 0.5ЭҢ. Э‘., first and second steps (SCC Step 1-2) connected and 
last below 0.5ЭҢ. Э‘., all three steps (SCC Step 1-2-3) connected.  
==PAGE:132==
The capacitor bank size to give required support is 3.75 times larger than the nominal 
power of VSC. Therefore, it may be seen as nonrealistic, nonetheless, cases are analyzed 
with and without capacitors for comparison. 
There are four level of short-circuit; at the first level, the PCC voltage below than ЬёаҜ•аҜҹаҜўаҜ–аҜһ 
and fault is lasting for 150ЭүЭҸ; at the second level PCC voltage is around 0.5ЭҢ. Э‘., and 
the faultвҖҷs lasting for 950ЭүЭҸ, for both level simulations done with and without capacitor 
banks, because the voltage level is below than 0.7ЭҢ. Э‘. At the third level PCC voltage is 
just above than 0.7ЭҢ. Э‘. and fault is lasting only 490ЭүЭҸ, due to stability limitation; At the 
last level PCC voltage is above than ЬёаҜҷаҜ”аҜЁаҜҹаҜ§, around 0.92ЭҢ. Э‘., at normal operation range 
and lasting 1.5ЭҸ; however, with this level, the behavior of VSCs is wanted to be simulated. 
All short-circuit cases are lasted 45ЭҸ and the fault is occurring at Эҗ= 10ЭҸ. For the last 
level of fault (Fault-4) active power control mode is changing to FSM control mode, with 
frequency droop is equal 6% and without dead-band, at Эҗ= 5ЭҸ. 
9.2.4 Model (Small Signal) Analysis 
The target with model analysis is to check the selected Base Control Mode for Active 
Power, after conducting analyses in previous sections, whether also stable for small 
disturbances or not.  
This analysis is conducted with DigSilentвҖҷs Model Analysis tool via using calculation 
method is вҖңQR/QZ-Method_QR Method using system reductionвҖқ. 
9.3 Results of Simulations 
9.3.1 Large Disturbance 
Analyses for defining base control mode and its parameters for active power control will 
be introduced. 
9.3.1.1 FSM: different frequency droops 
In this section red lines indicate, that frequency droop is equal to 6%, green lines 12% 
and last blue 3%. Small oscillations are due to active power control mode change, from 
Mode-0 to Mode-2, at Эҗ= 20ЭҸ. 
For all frequency droops, frequency remains within limits higher than 47ЬӘЭ– (0.94ЭҢ. Э‘.) 
and less than 60ЭҸ below 49ЬӘЭ– (0.98ЭҢ. Э‘.) [8]. Although 12% and 6% are reaching same 
frequency level, in terms of frequency response, 12% has the best performance because 
less frequency deviation.

the disturbance at frequency is much higher than this dead-level. It is better to test effect 
of implementing a dead-band with recurring but different size of disturbances.

9.3.1.3 Synthetic Inertia: different HdcвҖҷs 
As explained at the Section 9.2.1, the calculated value of synthetic inertia droop (Hdc) by 
the equation (6-40) is 1; however, when this value selected as Hdc parameter, simulation 
cannot find a convergent solution until increasing threshold an unreasonable high value 
to 0.31 (15.5ЬӘЭ–/ЭҸ), instead of 0.0007 (0.035ЬӘЭ–/ЭҸ) given in [1]. This threshold can only 
be satisfied, when Hdc is selected as 0.25. 
Before searching reason behind, it is crucial to emphasis some points, Synthetic Inertia 
block, whose details is given at the Section 6.1.2.5.4, is using built-in derivative block, 
which is using ЭҖЭҗ= 0.01ЭүЭҸ, and unlike physical inertia, for Synthetic Inertia a 40ЬӘЭ– 
duty cycle (5ЭүЭҸ вҖ“ on 20ЭүЭҸ off) is defined; last rather than changes, oscillating with high 
frequency, linear change trend on frequency is more the subject of Synthetic Inertia 
support. 
If the effect or manipulation of Synthetic Inertia is high enough to dominate on system 
frequency, a convergency problem should occur due to used derivative block, which 
creates a high-frequency oscillation.  
A prevention mechanism may be to filter high frequency component in the frequency 
before taking it into block definition. Because, as highlighted, the trend is important, the 
filtered signal can fulfill its duty.  
45,00
39,00
33,00
27,00
21,00

==PAGE:137==

117 
Instead of designing a new block for filtering there is a filtered frequency signal, which 
is an output of PLL_wf, details at 6.1.2.7.2. It has a low-pass filter with a cut-off 
frequency 100ЬӘЭ–. ItвҖҷs also suitable for 40ЬӘЭ– duty cycle of Synthetic Inertia support, as 
well as, it has been showed in previous chapters, that trends of PLL frequency and voltage 
measurement elementвҖҷs frequency similar, especially cases with synchronous generator. 
After using PL_wf as source of frequency the threshold value of 0.0007 (0.035ЬӘЭ–/ЭҸ) 
has been satisfied for Hdc values not only 1 but also 2. So, ЬӘЭҖЬҝ= 0.25 is used with 
regular PLL and ЬӘЭҖЬҝ= 1&2 are used with PLL_wf. 
In this section, red lines indicate, that synthetic inertia droop is equal to 0.25 with PLL, 
green lines 1 with PLL_wf and last blue 2 with PLL_wf.

9.3.1.4 FSM вҖ“ Synthetic Inertia вҖ“ Constant Power Modes

9.3.3 Short-Circuit 
After analysis of results, taken by Large Disturbance and Load Rejection cases, Mode-2 
is selected as base control mode; and 6% frequency droop and no dead-band as base 
parameter of this control mode, even though at first 3 Fault Cases, Control Modes 
supporting active power are prohibited due to fault levels. 
9.3.3.1 FRT & Overvoltage 
The color code of the Figure 9-25 is, that red lines represents the case Fault-1, below 
blocking voltage (~0.1ЭҢ. Э‘.), green lines the case Fault-2 (~0.5ЭҢ. Э‘.), blue lines the case 
Fault-3 (~0.7ЭҢ. Э‘.), and last pink lines the case Fault-4, where the PCC voltage stays 
within operational range [8].  
Fault-Ride-Through duration for Slave_PWM in case of those level of faults or voltage 
dips are derived from EnerginetвҖҷs regulations [34] and [35]. Before simulations 
expectations about durations are 150ЭүЭҸ for Fault-1, 950ЭүЭҸ for Fault-2, 1220ЭүЭҸ for 
Fault-3 and 1500ЭүЭҸ for Fault-4. 
Except the case Fault-3, expectations for other cases are satisfied, as seen at the Figure 
9-25. For Fault-3 only 490ЭүЭҸ fault duration is satisfied with existing grid properties.
