9.3.3.2 Short-Circuit Power during Faults 
There is interesting result in Short-Circuit Power flow through AC Line, which should 
trigger overcurrent protection. For the Figure 9-36, color coding is same with the Figure 
9-25, and straight lines indicate without Capacitor Banks and dashed lines with Capacitor 
Banks situations. 
In a classical grid, because short-circuit power is considered constant for a definite instant, 
roughly current increases along voltage sag getting worse. In grids under penetration of 
static sources, behavior of current is same with classical grid until a critical voltage level, 
beyond this level some sources in the grid are losing their constant power characteristic 
and becoming either a current source or impedance source. 
This phenomenon can partially be observed here with our 4 Fault cases. The power during 
faults flows through the AC Line has increased from the voltage level 92% (Fault-4) to 
70% (Fault-3); however, current starts decreasing after the 70% and itвҖҷs coming to almost 
same level with 92% at 50%. And this trend continues drastically both because of 
Slave_PWM blocked after at 40% and voltage drop. 
The effect of added capacitor banks during voltage drop can be observed here. Especially, 
for the case Fault-2, theyвҖҷve increased the power around 1.5 times more. 
For numerical and rough evaluation overcurrent protection performance, if the LoadвҖҷs 
nominal power is considered as 850ЬҜЬёЬЈ, there would be problems for cases Fault-4 and 
Fault-2 (without capacitor) on sensing faults at transmission level only with overcurrent 
protection. And for the case Fault-1 (with or without capacitors), it would be impossible 
to sense only with overcurrent protection.

9.3.4 Model (Small Signal) Analysis 
After the situation, faced during analysis of Fault-3 case, the Model Analysis is also used 
to trace back signs of insufficient grid strength at Master_Grid side, beyond examining 
the small signal stability of selected Base Control Mode for Active Power.  
As mentioned in the previous Section, 9.3.3, the base control selected Mode-2 with 6% 
frequency droop and no dead-band.  
For comparison purposes, Model Analysis is conducted for two cases, at the first case itвҖҷs 
kept initial SCR (6.1) of Master_Grid and at the second case it has been increased to 9.8 
same as done in Fault-3 case. 
At the beginning, all Eigenvalues of both Master_Grid cases are in stable range, there 
isnвҖҷt small-signal instable situation for selected control mode and grid conditions. At the 
Figure Figure 9-39, there are Eigenvalue Plots for critical modes, in terms of damping 
and damping ratio, of both Master_Grid cases. It can be seen, that a Mode in the stronger 
Master_Grid case has slightly better than weaker Master_Grid case.

==PAGE:156==
10 
 
CONCLUSION 
10.1 Results 
There are some results which are considered worthful to be highlighted: 
For smooth start to simulation in DigSilent PowerFactory, it is important to trace back 
values coming from load-flow calculation and to be careful of those values passing 
through blocks, because composite frames are closed-cycle; blocks can be individually 
correct but can contradict with information flow within composite frame. 
Even though there isnвҖҷt any convergent solution in simulation, it doesnвҖҷt always mean 
that no-operational point exists in physical system. 
If the size of Synthetic Inertia support is considerably high to be able to manipulate grid 
frequency, cyclic operation for Synthetic Inertia support is recommended in case of rate 
of frequency change exceeds threshold; and frequency should become input of it after 
passing through a low-pass filter. 
Although, only with one pair of control modes for each converter in Section 9.3.3.1 are 
used for FRT capability assessment of the generic controller model, it seems FRT 
capability of a VSC HVDC is closely related with the strength of both grids, and at least 
one of grids should be strong in classical way.  
According to results given in the Section 8.3.4, compensation in lower levels, for instance 
in distribution level, is important for performance of weak grid. 
In [12], besides guidance of modelling, a discussion about the integration step is stated 
for computational performance due to very fast dynamics of power electronic device. The 
switching frequency of VSCs is considered in this work as 2ЭҮЬӘЭ–, means 0.5ЭүЭҸ switching 
period, and required PI gains, except PLLвҖҷs, are calculated according to this frequency. 
Therefore, integration step choices above 0.25ЭүЭҸ couldnвҖҷt manage to compute a 
convergent value during most of events. In some cases, even smaller step size may be 
required.  
==PAGE:157==
 
 
10.2 Future Work 
There are some possibilities for further works: 
Since in RMS Simulation, voltage inputs of controller model are RMS values, supplied 
by virtual voltage measurement device within DigSilent, but in a similar way with a 
physical analyzer, selection methodology of Current Controller (Inner-Loop) blockвҖҷs PI 
gains, in frequency domain, can be further investigated. Moreover, PLLвҖҷs meaningful 
bandwidth is highly related with sampling rate of source, where voltage measurement are 
coming. 
In the beginning, the aim was making analyses in all or part of EnerginetвҖҷs grid; however, 
analyses were bounded with a basic weak grid due timing, caused by not only complexity 
of EnerginetвҖҷs grid model, but also requirement of modelling & verifying the generic 
controller. For future work, the model can be used for real system analysis, e.g. for 
EnerginetвҖҷs grid. Nevertheless, Slave_Grid part of the grid, which given in the Chapter 8, 
might be considered a highly simplified representation of an introduced model of 
Energinet in [36]. 
The generic controller modelвҖҷs applicability to a real physical system and convenience of 
responses, especially about Synthetic Inertia mode, can be another next step of this work. 
Commitment schedule shifts of generation units at the beginning of each hour due to 
market transactions are threating frequency containment reserves (FCR) because 
discontinuities of operational set points lead fluctuations in frequency. As a later work 
Synthetic Inertia support, combined with an adaptive constant DC Voltage control mode 
at the other converter, can be tested for handling this transient disturbance. 
10.3 Perspective (Glance to Future) 
As a conclusion of this report, I would like to share some topics reflecting my glance to 
future grid: 
According to given results in the Section 9.3.3.2,  even VSC HVDC can contribute to 
short-circuit for some degree, itвҖҷs not as much as traditional generatorвҖҷs short circuit 
current. So, overcurrent protection wonвҖҷt be alone enough to sense fault, if grids will be 
split via DC/AC converter to smaller grids and/or generation sources connected to 
backbone of system with again DC/AC converters. A new protection philosophy, based 
on combination of current and voltage profiles, not meaning distance protection, might 
be a solution. 
Simulations, with synchronous generator, were done for time frame of 45ЭҸвҲ’90ЭҸ, where 
elapsed time of calculations, with 0.25ЭүЭҸ integration step and without using an adaptive 
algorithm to increase steps, were between 2/3 and 5/6 of time frame for ins. Even though 
==PAGE:158==
grids are not complicated, used hardware for simulation is more than 4 years old laptop 
with limited performance. I believe, if simulation program is enough robust to handle 
with nonlinearity problems, occurred due to complexity of grid and causing divergency, 
elapsed time wonвҖҷt be matter in terms of very small integration steps because of advanced 
technology in HW. 
Investigated issues and events in the Chapter 7, unevenly paralleled power lines and 
frequent wrong-maneuver in power system shouldnвҖҷt be common problem for future grid. 
In different countries, deregulation in power market generally started splitting 
transmission, distribution and generation activities. After first step, market operation, 
transmission & generation system operation, transmission assetsвҖҷ O&M and regulatory 
duties have mostly remained at Transmission company side. In further steps, market 
operation and regulatory duties have been taken over by other authorities. However, 
transmission asset O&M as well as power system operation are still transmission 
companyвҖҷs responsibility in most countries. 
If VSC HVDCвҖҷs successfulness in operation and increment in their number lead both 
introduction of new ancillary services in power market and splitting existing transmission 
systems into sub-transmission parties, separation of asset operation and system operation 
duties will be unavoidable. And System Operator may be a supervisor of whole system 
unlike being only a Transmission System Operator, where distribution systems are 
becoming important for voltage & frequency control with distributed sources. This 
transformation will take time due to low asset turnover rates and slow development on 
professional competencies to afford this change, although technology is advancing rapid 
and regulations are trying catch technology development.
